### 42nd-pass open questions (2026-07-02, this run)

| #    | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Status                         | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         |

| R151 | **Probe loop concurrency limit** — the runtime enforces a 1-concurrent-subagent-per-role limit during probe dispatch despite the `run_scope_probes` job instructions saying max 3; concurrent spawns beyond 1 are rejected with `duplicate_subagent_for_step`. The 42nd-pass probe loop attempted a concurrent batch of 3; only 1 (kanban-dispatch-orphan-reconciliation) succeeded; the other 2 were rejected, and the loop fell back to serial dispatch for the remaining 6 scopes. Future bootstrap cycles should plan for serial dispatch by default (per-scope subagent), with a best-effort concurrent spawn only for the first subagent. This is a runtime-level constraint, not a project code constraint — but it materially affects bootstrap wall-clock time for large manifests.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Open (operational)             | Recommendation: update the `run_scope_probes` job instructions to set `max_concurrent_subagents_per_role: 1` and serialize by default. The R25/R30 escalation sequence for the 5 still-failed split-retries is unaffected by this constraint. |
| R152 | **memory-drift-detection — no standalone unit tests for the 5 extracted helper modules** (`memory-drift-checkers.ts`, `memory-drift-reference.parser.ts`, `memory-drift-indexes.ts`, `memory-drift-persistence.ts`, `memory-drift.coercion.ts`). The service spec exercises them transitively, but a pure-function unit test on each (e.g., file checker `path_outside_repo`, API checker regex escaping, parser's three-way classification, index build on partial metadata, coercers' malformed-input fallbacks) would lock the helper contracts more durably. Recommendation: file a low-priority followup to extract these spec files mirroring `memory-decay.classify.spec.ts` / `memory-decay.value-predicate.spec.ts`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Open (coverage)                | Compare with the decay reaper's `memory-decay.classify.spec.ts` and `memory-decay.value-predicate.spec.ts` which DO have dedicated unit tests for similar extracted helpers.                                                                  |
| R153 | **memory-drift-detection — gaps in dedicated processor + metric specs**: no dedicated `memory-drift.processor.spec.ts` for the BullMQ processor's job-name dispatch (`_job.name !== MEMORY_DRIFT_JOB_NAME` returns `null`) and per-tick wrapper logging; `recordMemoryDriftDetected(...)` and `nexusMemoryDriftDetectedTotal` are not directly asserted in `metrics.service.spec.ts`; no direct unit test for the `recheck_after_ms = undefined` short-circuit. Also: `memory_drift_recheck_after_ms` is absent from `system-settings.defaults.ts` (the absence of the setting is the documented signal "skip drifted rows"); no `docs/guide/memory-drift-detection.md` deep-dive entry (only EPIC-212 + superpowers/plans references).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Open (coverage + docs)         | The drift integration test's `INTEGRATION_TEST_DATABASE_URL` gate is correct but requires CI to provision a dedicated throwaway DB.                                                                                                           |
| R154 | **oauth-redis-durable-session — ADR Follow-ups still deferred**: (a) BullMQ worker migration — true restart-and-resume of the in-flight `provider.login` Promise (the durable Redis shape is the substrate for this future worker); (b) `session_taken_over_at` audit field — no audit signal recorded when a session's transient half is rebound; (c) `nexus_oauth_login_orphaned_total` Prometheus counter — orphan-recovery path is silent in dashboards today. Owner TBD per ADR. **Also**: pre-existing `oauth-login-service.md` artifact is now stale (describes pre-refactor `SESSION_TTL_MS`, `CLEANUP_INTERVAL_MS`, and `Map<string, LoginSession>` shape); a follow-up edit should cross-reference the new 53b39246 artifact and remove stale descriptions.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                | Open (ADR follow-ups)          | The 900-second TTL enforcement + orphan recovery + cross-pod delivery are all in production today; only the ADR-deferred items remain.                                                                                                        |
| R155 | **runtime-feedback — minor cleanup + UX gaps**: (a) `runtime-feedback-diagnostics.service.types.ts` is an unused, slightly divergent copy of the response interface (missing `windowOccurrenceCount` + `windowStartedAt` but includes `dedupeFingerprint`); consumers use the schema-inferred type from `runtime-feedback-diagnostics.types.ts`. (b) Diagnostic flow projects away `evidence_json` / `examples_json` / `diagnostics_json`, but there is no `GET /runtime-feedback/groups/:id` deep-dive endpoint for operators to inspect why a particular group was skipped — out of scope per closeout plan. (c) `workflow_anomaly` producer wiring location needs confirmation (suspected `workflow-step-execution` or `workflow-repair`, not `runtime-feedback` itself).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Open (cleanup + UX)            | Low-priority followups; the module is feature-complete and end-to-end tested.                                                                                                                                                                 |
| R156 | **learning-convergence-feedback — coverage + board-state gaps**: (a) No direct unit tests for `computeConvergenceSnapshots` (the helper is reachable only via `memory-metrics.service.spec.ts` which mixes convergence math with metrics plumbing). (b) No direct unit tests for `LearningMeasurementState` (the `MAX_ARM_RING_PER_SCOPE = 100_000` cap, the probation record, and `setCostPerPromotedMemory` numeric coercion branches each have one-line contract changes currently shielded only by integration tests). (c) No direct unit tests for `classifyDecay` (drift-acceleration branch in Task 4 lives here). (d) **88d7654e board status** remains `backlog` despite the code being implemented end-to-end; orchestrator has repeatedly auto-cleared the in-progress marker due to no linked workflow run. **Recommendation**: follow-up probe against `workflow-step-execution/step-support.service.ts`, the WebUI's `MemoryHealthCard`, and the integration spec to confirm the full work-item surface is exercised; reconcile kanban status with code reality.                                                                                                                                                       | Open (coverage + board)        | Confidence deduction 0.10 (from 0.96 to 0.86) reflects these coverage-only gaps.                                                                                                                                                              |
| R157 | **memory-segment-feedback-channel — path discrepancy + missing spec**: (a) Playbook path `apps/api/src/memory/learning/learning-convergence.helper.ts` is incorrect; actual location is `apps/api/src/memory/learning-convergence.helper.ts` (one level above the `learning/` subdirectory). The same discrepancy was flagged by the prior `learning-convergence-feedback` probe (R156). (b) Missing dedicated unit-test for `MemorySegmentFeedbackService` (header comment promises a "milestone 4" unit spec that has not landed); the service's `normaliseReason` trim + 2_000-char cap, audit-emit best-effort swallow, segment-source fallback to `null`, settings-service swallow with default fall-through are uncovered by direct unit assertions. The constants file (`memory-decay.constants.ts`) explicitly references work item 3d7fb798 and exports `MEMORY_DECAY_EXEMPT_SOURCES` (a `ReadonlySet<string>` containing `learning_candidate`, `workflow_failure_postmortem`, `strategic_intent` — the three sources that must NEVER be decayed out of the active set). `memory-decay.reaper.ts` is a NestJS `@Injectable` service (~626 lines) that scans the memory-segment table for decay candidates, applies a configurable daily decay rate with a grace window and a confidence floor, and archives rows that fall below the floor. The integration spec (`memory-decay.reaper.integration.spec.ts`, 713+ lines) exercises the reaper end-to-end with a hand-rolled in-memory `MemorySegmentRepository` that faithfully implements the production SQL filter, seeding 10 memory segments across 3 non-exempt sources and asserting exactly 4 archived / 6 retained with correct per-row decay math (`confidence = 0.8 - 0.01 * 30 = 0.5` for a 60-day-old segment with a 30-day grace window and a 0.01 daily rate). | R105 | **`memory-decay-reaper` (3d7fb798, confidence 0.9) — missing BullMQ consumer for `MEMORY_DECAY_QUEUE`.** The reaper service registers a repeatable job on `MEMORY_DECAY_QUEUE` with the name `MEMORY_DECAY_JOB_NAME` via `OnApplicationBootstrap → scheduleDecayJob()`, but a grep across `apps/api/src` finds **no `@Processor('memory-decay')` (or equivalent) consumer** registered to invoke `runDecayPass()` when the cron tick fires. Compare this with the eviction reaper, which has a dedicated `memory-eviction.processor.ts` with a `@Processor(MEMORY_EVICTION_QUEUE)` decorator. The reaper service's own docstring describes `runDecayPass()` as "the test-friendly seam: it is a pure method that can be invoked from a BullMQ processor, an admin trigger handler, or a unit test" — so the missing processor may be deferred to a follow-up milestone (the constants file's docstring even mentions "The BullMQ scheduler milestone will add a processor on this queue."). At runtime today, the cron-registered job would sit in the queue without a consumer; operators would need to invoke `runDecayPass()` manually (e.g., via an admin endpoint) for the reaper to actually run. **Recommendation**: file a follow-up work item to add a `memory-decay.processor.ts` with a `@Processor('memory-decay')` consumer. Compare with the eviction reaper pattern at `apps/api/src/memory/memory-eviction.processor.ts`. | Open     | The decay-reaper in-main implementation is otherwise complete (11 unit tests + full integration suite) — this is the only implementation gap. The constants file's docstring notes "The BullMQ scheduler milestone will add a processor on this queue", which suggests the missing processor is intentionally deferred to a follow-up milestone rather than a bug. The next CEO cycle should: (1) confirm whether the BullMQ processor is intentionally deferred to a follow-up work item or whether it is a gap that needs to be filed now; (2) when ready, file a work item to add `memory-decay.processor.ts` mirroring the eviction reaper's pattern.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                |
| R106 | **`memory-token-budget-resolver` (ddfdcead, confidence 0.96) — no dedicated docs entry for the new env knobs.** The four files in scope (`memory-token-budget.resolver.ts`, `memory-token-budget.resolver.types.ts`, `memory-token-budget.resolver.spec.ts`, `memory-token-budget.integration.spec.ts`), the `MemoryModule` factory wiring, and the consumer-side defensive wrappers are all well-commented in code, but there is no `docs/architecture/` or `docs/guide/` entry that walks an operator through the new env knobs end-to-end (defaults, valid ranges, interaction with `DistillationThresholdService`, expected values for 8k/128k/200k models). A short guide entry would close that loop and is independent of any code change.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | Resolved | Resolved by work item `2fffd172-d5a1-41bd-a4d3-ec9c9f7e52c4` (WI-2026-053) — see [`docs/guide/memory-token-budget-resolver.md`](../../guide/memory-token-budget-resolver.md) for the new operator-facing entry (env-knob table, default 60/30/10 slice, worked examples for 8k / 128k / 200k / 1M context windows, fallback semantics, and the R107/R108/R111 followups). | R107 | **`memory-token-budget-resolver` (ddfdcead) — ConfigService validation schema not yet declared for the `MEMORY_BUDGET_*` env keys.** The `readBudgetOptions` helper in `MemoryModule` uses loose `config.get` + `??` coercion because the API env validation schema does not declare `MEMORY_BUDGET_MEMORY_PERCENT` / `MEMORY_BUDGET_WORKING_PERCENT` / `MEMORY_BUDGET_RESERVED_PERCENT` / `MEMORY_BUDGET_FALLBACK_CONTEXT_WINDOW`. Promoting these to first-class validated env keys (with a Zod schema entry) is a followup hygiene task — the resolver works without it but operators have no validation feedback for typos.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Open     | The schema is `apps/api/src/config/env.validation.ts` (or equivalent). The followup is to add a Zod schema entry for the four `MEMORY_BUDGET_*` keys with `coerce.number().int().min(0).max(100)` for the percentages and `coerce.number().int().positive()` for the fallback window. Low-risk hygiene task.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| R108 | **`memory-token-budget-resolver` (ddfdcead) — reserved-slice semantics could be misleading at extreme configurations.** With `memoryPercent=1, workingPercent=1, reservedPercent=1` the integration test asserts `reserved = 196_000` (98%). Operators who think of `reservedPercent` as a hard ceiling on system overhead may be surprised when it silently absorbs the unallocated remainder. A future enhancement could optionally throw or warn when `memoryPercent + workingPercent + reservedPercent < 100` to make the implicit remainder visible. Not a bug today; just a future ergonomic improvement.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Open     | The current behavior is documented in the JSDoc on `slice`: "memory and working are computed with Math.floor to ensure conservative allocation; reserved absorbs any rounding remainder". The behaviour is correct for the documented contract but a UX-level "warn on implicit remainder" enhancement would surface the gap. No urgent action; consider for the next major revision of the resolver.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                    |
| R109 | **`memory-decay-reaper` (3d7fb798) — settings runtime mutation flow.** The constants file and `SystemSettingsService` describe an "operator updates the cron expression" → "next bootstrap re-reads the value" flow, but the reaper service does not currently subscribe to settings-change events to re-register the repeatable job mid-process. A cron change today would only take effect after the next application restart. This matches the eviction reaper's behavior, but is worth flagging if "live cron update without restart" is a desired capability.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Open     | The behavior is consistent with the eviction reaper and the broader NestJS-BullMQ cron pattern; live cron update is a known limitation. If live cron update becomes a desired capability, a follow-up work item would be needed to subscribe to settings-change events and call `BullMQ.cancelRepeatable()` + `scheduleDecayJob()` on change. No urgent action.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| R110 | **`memory-decay-reaper` (3d7fb798) — decay-in-place path type ergonomics.** The reaper documents that `QueryDeepPartialEntity<MemorySegment>` does not accept a `Record<string, unknown>` shape for `metadata_json` (because of how the partial-entity helper unwraps nested objects) and works around this by mutating the loaded entity and calling `repository.save(segment)`. This is correct for the current schema but creates a hidden dependency on TypeORM's reflection metadata shape — a future migration that introduces stricter typed columns on `metadata_json` could surface the same friction elsewhere.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Open     | The workaround is correct for the current schema and tested in the integration suite. If `metadata_json` becomes a structured-typed column in a future migration, the workaround may need to be revisited. Document the workaround in the service's JSDoc; consider adding a typing test to lock the shape. No urgent action.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            |
| R111 | **`memory-token-budget-resolver` (ddfdcead) — `getModelForUseCase` is the entry point, not `getActiveModel`.** The resolver queries by `useCase` (defaulting to `'distillation'`), so a model change at runtime flows through `AiConfigurationService`'s DB-backed `agent_profiles` table — not through environment variables. Operators expecting env-driven model selection should be pointed at the precedence chain documented in `AGENTS.md` ("Workflow step override → Agent profile → DB default → env fallback"). Not a bug; just a discoverability note worth adding to a docs entry.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                            | Resolved | Resolved by work item `9b3b1563-e167-4a18-b59c-3fd177d464c2` (WI-2026-056) — see the new "How runtime model selection reaches the resolver" subsection in [`docs/guide/memory-token-budget-resolver.md`](../../guide/memory-token-budget-resolver.md) for the operator-facing enumeration of the four precedence levels (workflow step override → agent profile → DB default model for use case → env fallback) with inline citations to `AGENTS.md` and the `getModelForUseCase(...)` method on `apps/api/src/ai-config/database/repositories/llm-model.repository.ts`, and a worked example for swapping the distillation model to a 200k context variant. Also discoverable from `apps/api/README.md` → "Provider Setup" → "Provider References" (cross-link). The probe narrative at `docs/project-context/probe-results/memory-token-budget-resolver.md` → "Open Questions" has also been updated with the same resolution pointer. |

### 8th-pass probe follow-up questions (2026-06-16)

| #   | Topic                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                               | Status | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| --- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | ------ | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ |
| R40 | The `DistillationJobData` interface in `apps/api/src/memory/distillation.consumer.ts:16-17` still carries `threshold?: number; thresholdSource?: string;` but the consumer no longer reads them — it resolves fresh on every tick via `DistillationThresholdService.resolve(sessionTreeId)`. Whether to prune these legacy fields or keep them for back-compat with producers that still set them is a followup cleanup question, not a correctness issue.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Open   | The 8th-pass probe flagged this as a followup cleanup. The fields are unused on the read path; removing them is a minor breaking change for any external producers that set them. Recommend pruning in a followup commit if no external producers exist.                                   |
| R41 | `DistillationThresholdService` keeps `lastValue` and `lastSource` as instance state, so the change-detection cache is per-service-instance. With NestJS singleton scope this is one cache per process. In a multi-process deployment (BullMQ workers + API server) the per-process cache means each process will independently observe and emit `MemorySettingChanged` events for its first tick after a SystemSetting change. This is the documented intent (the resolver is the source of truth; the cache is just an optimisation to suppress redundant events), and the EventLedger events are deduplicated downstream by `(key, previousValue, newValue)` rather than by source, so it is operationally fine — but worth flagging in case the consumer of these events ever assumes single-emission semantics. | Open   | Documented in the probe as an operational fine-print, not a bug. If single-emission semantics are needed in the future, the cache would need to be lifted to a shared store (Redis) or the per-process cache would need to be paired with a leader-election scheme.                        |
| R42 | Adding `DistillationThresholdService` to the `SessionHydrationService` constructor may have downstream test-fixture implications in `session-hydration.service.spec.ts` and the various `__tests__/agent-await.integration.spec.ts` / `step-required-tool-retry.service.spec.ts` / `workflow-await.module.spec.ts` / `subagent-*.spec.ts` style tests that provide `SessionHydrationService` directly via `useValue`. The 8th-pass probe confirmed `session-hydration.service.spec.ts` already injects a mock `distillationThreshold` with `resolve: vi.fn().mockResolvedValue({ value: 0.8, source: 'default' })`. The other downstream test suites were not in the assigned scope.                                                                                                                                | Open   | Recommend running `pnpm test` on the next CI cycle to confirm all downstream test suites compile cleanly with the new constructor parameter. Not a blocker for 3effbfa9 — the source compiles cleanly per the probe.                                                                       |
| R43 | The API `DistillationOutcome = 'success' \| 'failure' \| 'skipped'` (apps/api/src/memory/memory-metrics.types.ts:11) includes `'skipped'` (the new "under live threshold" skip path), but the web `MemoryMetricsDistillationOutcome = "success" \| "failure"` (apps/web/src/lib/api/memory.types.ts:90) omits it. The card only iterates the two booleans, so `'skipped'` is silently excluded from the web view. The web types file has a JSDoc comment marking the snapshot as a verbatim mirror of the API types file, which is a deliberate "keep both files in sync" warning.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Open   | Not a current functional break (the API never emits `'skipped'` in production yet — the 3effbfa9 work item's `recordThresholdSkip` path is the first producer), but the divergence is intentional from the web side. Product/UX intent for the skipped outcome is unclear from code alone. |
| R44 | The per-backend `fallback` map in `MemoryMetricsResponse.backend.fallback` (e.g. `postgres->honcho:read`) is captured in the type but not rendered by `MemoryHealthCard`. Likely intentional for now, but worth confirming whether the operator-facing surface should expose the fallback transition rate.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Open   | Not a blocker for 1e5b3af0 — the data is captured and the card surface is the minimum useful display. Product/UX intent for the fallback visualization is unclear from code alone.                                                                                                         |
| R45 | The 1e5b3af0 work item's "Acceptance" line requires "dashboard renders live counts" and "counters increment under integration test" — the API integration test (`memory-metrics.service.spec.ts`, 7.1KB, 2026-06-16 16:06) exists but was not in the assigned 8th-pass scope. The 8th-pass consumer-plane spec confirms renderability of a mocked snapshot but does not exercise the polling loop end-to-end.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       | Open   | Recommend verifying in the next CI cycle that an integration test wires `ControlPlaneBoard` to a real API and exercises the 30s polling loop. Not a blocker for 1e5b3af0 — the data-plane integration test is sufficient for the service layer.                                            |

| --- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------- |
| 1   | opencode binary (`OPencode_PATH`) must be available in execution environment — no bundled fallback or validation                           | Medium   |
| 2   | Docker rebuild depends on `docker compose` — no validation or error message if unavailable                                                 | Low      |
| 3   | Git push requires `GITHUB_TOKEN`/`GH_TOKEN`/`GIT_TOKEN` — service fails without them if repairs succeed but push fails                     | Medium   |
| 4   | Telemetry WebSocket reconnection with `reconnectionAttempts: Infinity` — long-term behavior under persistent connection failures undefined | Low      |
| 5   | `RepairAgentAPI` does not authenticate requests — any client can update repair logs or query sessions                                      | High     |

---

The kernel registry is "register-once" via `Map` overwrite, so double-imports are idempotent but the intent is implicit. Worth documenting or hardening.                                                                                                                                                                   | Low                                                                                                                      | harness-runtime, harness-engine-pi, harness-engine-claude-code |

## Newly Discovered Open Questions (2026-06-15 Retry Cycle)

### GitOps Reconciliation Core

| #   | Question                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   | Priority | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| --- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| G1  | ✅ **RESOLVED** — `GitOpsReconciliationLoopService.tick()` is wired with a scheduled interval (`GITOPS_RECONCILIATION_INTERVAL_MS` + `GITOPS_RECONCILIATION_JITTER_MS` jitter) and invokes the canonical `GitOpsInboundReconcileService.apply(scopeNodeId, bindingId, actor)` per active binding. Is `GitOpsReconciliationLoop` intended to be wired via a lifecycle hook (e.g. `OnModuleInit` in a separate `GitOpsLoopService`) or whether scheduling has been intentionally deferred? The class and its spec are present, the `intervalMs` config exists, but no provider or lifecycle wiring exists in `GitOpsModule`. | High     | **Resolved by** [WI-2026-059](../work-items/WI-2026-059-wire-gitops-reconciliation-loop-per-binding.md). `GitOpsInboundReconcileService.apply()` is now the only mutation path; `ReconciliationService.apply()` is a deprecated adapter that emits `gitops.reconciliation.deprecated_apply` and delegates. The loop is wired to the inbound service per active binding. |
| G2  | Is `config_override` apply intentionally deferred or blocked on a design decision? Override source policy, conflict policy, and merge/replace semantics live in `packages/gitops-contracts/overrides.schema.ts` but are not yet exercised end-to-end.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | High     | Applier throws `Error('config_override apply not yet implemented for key: ...')`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                       |
| G3  | Is the integration test (`reconciliation.integration.spec.ts`) exercised in CI? The `DATABASE_URL` gate means it is silently skipped in any environment without a Postgres reachable, and the spec uses a standalone `DataSource` factory rather than the shared test database setup.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Medium   | Currently `describe.skipIf(!DB_AVAILABLE)`.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| G4  | Should the `ReconciliationService.apply()` thin wrapper (which hardcodes `dryRun: false`) be retained, or should all apply flows go through `GitOpsInboundReconcileService.apply()` (which passes `bindingId`/`conflictPolicy` and is the only path that records a `GitOpsReconcileRun` row)?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Medium   | Two apply entry points; choice has audit-log implications.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |
| G5  | Is the `apply()` transaction's per-change audit-log pattern sufficient for forensic needs? The audit row is written _after_ the DB write succeeds, so a crash between the write and the audit would leave a silent change.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 | Low      | Documented as a latent gap.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             |
| G6  | Is the diff engine's silent skip of desired-state objects that exist in DB under non-gitops ownership the desired UX? The comment says "intentionally skipped with no output", but a real reconcile against a polluted DB could mask ownership conflicts.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Low      | Latent UX gap.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |

### GitOps Desired State and Sync

| #   | Question                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                             | Priority | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| --- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| G7  | ✅ **RESOLVED** — Where is the `credentialsSecretId` on `GitOpsRepositoryBinding` consumed? The loader rejects URLs with embedded credentials, and the outbound sync uses `git` over HTTPS with no auth, so the column is currently a no-op.                                                                                                                                                                                                                         | High     | **Resolved by** WI-2026-061 (`feature/WI-2026-061-gitops-credentials-secret-id`). The column is now consumed by `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-credentials-resolver.service.ts` (60s in-memory TTL cache), wired through `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-invocation-builder.ts` into both `GitOpsOutboundSyncService` (push/fetch) and `DesiredStateLoaderService` (inbound desired-state load). HTTPS credentials are delivered via `GIT_CONFIG_*` env vars; SSH keys via `GIT_SSH_COMMAND` with a 0600 temp file. Strict-mode env var: `GITOPS_REQUIRE_CREDENTIALS` (default `false`). See `docs/architecture/gitops.md` for the design and AC traceability. |
| G8  | Should `POST /gitops/validate` be wired to `ConfigValidationService.lint` with a request-supplied directory, or is the per-binding variant the primary path going forward?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Medium   | Legacy endpoint returns 200 OK with a "not yet wired" message; should be 501.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| G9  | Is the `gitops-status.controller.ts` reference in the manifest a leftover (suggesting the file was once separate from `gitops.controller.ts` and was later merged) or a typo that should be cleaned up?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              | Low      | File is missing on disk; spec exercises `GitOpsController.getStatus` directly.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| G10 | Should `gitops_pending_changes` rows be surfaced through `GitOpsStatusService.drift` when `changeType !== 'drift'`? Currently only `changeType === 'drift'` produces a `DriftSummary`; pending changes of other types contribute only to `pendingChangeCount` and not to the `drift[]` array.                                                                                                                                                                        | Low      | Status-service behaviour gap.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           |
| G11 | Are `GitOpsEditPolicyService` and `GitOpsPendingChangeService` actually wired into the controllers of the resource types they protect? The services exist and are exported by the module, but the actual call sites are outside this probe's scope.                                                                                                                                                                                                                  | Medium   | Producer/consumer integration gap.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      |
| G12 | ✅ **RESOLVED** — The loop now invokes `GitOpsInboundReconcileService.apply(scopeNodeId, bindingId, actor)` per binding inside a per-binding `try`/`catch` and emits `gitops.reconciliation.tick_completed`. Should `GitOpsReconciliationLoop` (covered in `gitops-reconciliation-core.md`) call the binding-aware `GitOpsInboundReconcileService` or the env-driven `ReconciliationService` for each tick? Both are exported, the choice has security implications. | High     | **Resolved by** [WI-2026-059](../work-items/WI-2026-059-wire-gitops-reconciliation-loop-per-binding.md). `GitOpsInboundReconcileService.apply()` is now the only mutation path; `ReconciliationService.apply()` is a deprecated adapter that emits `gitops.reconciliation.deprecated_apply` and delegates. The loop is wired to the inbound service per active binding.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                 |
| G13 | Should the legacy env-driven `POST /gitops/reconcile` and `GET /gitops/drift` routes be deprecated now that per-binding sub-routes exist, or kept for backward compatibility?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                        | Low      | API surface decision.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                   |
| G14 | Should the hard-coded `manual: 0, seed: 0` in `GitOpsStatusService.getStatus` be backfilled by a query against the `managed_by` column on each reconciled table?                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     | Low      | Known limitation noted in the type.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                     |

The spec uses a subclass; comments explicitly defer the wiring decision.~~ **RESOLVED** by [WI-2026-064](../work-items/WI-2026-064-execution-ip-resolution-override.md) — the hook has been promoted to a typed `IOrchestratorIpResolver` DI token (`ORCHESTRATOR_IP_RESOLVER`) with a system-setting-driven strategy override (`default` / `dns_round_robin` / `service_mesh_header` / `custom_http_endpoint`); see [§2 Orchestrator IP Resolution Override (WI-2026-064)](../architecture/execution-lifecycle-supervisor.md#2-orchestrator-ip-resolution-override-wi-2026-064) in the architecture doc. | High     | **Resolved by** [WI-2026-064](../work-items/WI-2026-064-execution-ip-resolution-override.md). |

### Execution Lifecycle Persistence

| #   | Question                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          | Priority | Notes                                                                      |
| --- | --------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | -------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| E5  | Are the `workflow_step` and `workflow_chat` recovery paths actually exercised by `StartupResumeCoordinator` in production? The supervisor-scope probe found the resume coordinator's tests cover `paused`, `missing`, `running`, and `stopped` container states, but the rehydrator's "returns false" path is not in those tests. | Medium   | Worth confirming with the workflow-step-execution probe.                   |
| E6  | Is the `ExecutionProjector`'s non-subscription to `paused`/`resumed` events intentional (freeze is an emergency system-level action that should not be replayable from the outbox) or a missing projection?                                                                                                                       | Medium   | Freeze flag is written directly to the row via `markFrozen`/`clearFrozen`. |
| E7  | `subagent-container-liveness.probe.ts` has no paired spec. Its behavior is exercised through `ExecutionSupervisorService.sweepOnce()` tests, but a direct unit test for the probe's `isContainerLost()` response to `exited`/`dead`/`removing`/`404`/generic error paths would tighten the contract.                              | Low      | Currently covered by integration only.                                     |
| E8  | Does the repository's `applyTransition()` patch-passthrough on illegal transitions return `null` consistently? The repository spec asserts `save` is not called. Do downstream callers (e.g., the projector) check for `null` and emit a diagnostic event, or silently ignore the failure?                                        | Low      | Defensive warn-log in projector would help.                                |
| E9  | `ExecutionEntity.version` (`@VersionColumn()`) is declared but `applyTransition()` uses `findById` + `save` rather than `repository.update({ id, version }, …)`. The optimistic lock is effectively a no-op unless a future refactor changes the update path.                                                                     | Low      | Version column is currently passive.                                       |

### Memory System — Active Self-Improvement Loop Todos

| #   | Question                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                      | Priority | Notes                                       |
| --- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | ------------------------------------------- |
| M1  | Should the parent workflow file new work items for the 4 self-improvement-loop TODO items, or treat them as a deferred backlog? ### Kanban Retrospectives — Failure Threshold Trigger

| #   | Question                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | Priority | Notes                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                          |
| --- | ---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- | -------- | ------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------ | -------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------- |
| K1  | What constitutes a "failure" for threshold counting? The codebase has at least three failure surfaces with different granularities: a work-item workflow run (`work_item_workflow_run_failed` fact), an orchestration run (status transitions to `failed`), and Core event delivery failures (`event_delivery_failed` fact). The threshold semantics need a product-side decision. | High     | **Resolved by [WI-2026-062](WI-2026-062) (work item id `2a64258d-8542-4ca0-b582-42a69dd61ff0`) — Typed failure surface.** The `FailureClass` enum (in `@nexus/core`) classifies every failure as one of `QaRejection`, `NoActionableWork`, `SystemFailure`, `EventDeliveryFailure`, or `UnhandledException`; only the last three (per `FAILURE_CLASSES_THAT_COUNT` / `shouldCountFailure`) increment the consecutive-failure counter. The diagnostic `kanban.retrospective.failure_observed` event is emitted on every call (counted + non-counted) so the full surface is auditable. See [§9 Typed Failure Surface](../architecture/kanban-retrospective-cycle-decision-architecture.md#9-typed-failure-surface-wi-2026-062). |
| K2  | Should the failure-threshold trigger bypass the 15-minute cooldown or respect it? The current `executeRun` short-circuits on `cooldown_active` unless `manual_override === true`. A second setting or a dedicated idempotency-key scheme may be needed.                                                                                                                            | Medium   | **Resolved by [WI-2026-063](../work-items/WI-2026-063-failure-threshold-settings-schema.md) (work item id `2ec2799b-b003-4f5d-bca4-d56d3ef601dd`) — Cooldown bypass knob.** Introduced `retrospective_failure_threshold_bypass_cooldown` setting (boolean, default `false`); when `true`, the 15-minute cooldown is bypassed. When bypass is in effect, `KanbanRetrospectiveService.executeRun` emits a `kanban.retrospective.cooldown_skipped` diagnostic event carrying `bypassCooldown: true` and the deterministic `trigger_revision_marker` for audit. See [§10 Failure-Threshold Settings Schema](../architecture/kanban-retrospective-cycle-decision-architecture.md#10-failure-threshold-settings-schema-wi-2026-063). |
| K3  | Which event bus should the failure listener subscribe to? The kanban `EventEmitter2` singleton currently carries only the retrospective cycle decision event; failure facts are persisted to the control plane via `publishFact`, not emitted on the in-process bus.                                                                                                               | Medium   | Architecture decision (in-process bus vs control-plane fact scan vs polling).                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                  |
| K4  | What settings are required? At minimum, a count threshold and a time window. Possible keys: `retrospective_failure_threshold_enabled` (boolean), `retrospective_failure_threshold_count` (number, min 1, e.g. default 3), `retrospective_failure_threshold_window_seconds` (number, e.g. default 600).                                                                             | Medium   | **Resolved by [WI-2026-063](../work-items/WI-2026-063-failure-threshold-settings-schema.md) (work item id `2ec2799b-b003-4f5d-bca4-d56d3ef601dd`) — Settings schema.** Promoted the failure-threshold trigger's knobs to 6 typed `SystemSetting` entries with Zod validation: enabled (bool, default true), count (int 1-100, default 3), window_seconds (int 60-86400, default 600), cooldown_seconds (int 0-86400, default 900), bypass_cooldown (bool, default false), window_strategy ('sliding'                                                                                                                                                                                                                           | 'fixed', default 'sliding'). Defined in `@nexus/core` (`packages/core/src/retrospectives/failure-threshold-settings.constants.ts`) and validated in `apps/api` (`apps/api/src/settings/retrospective-failure-threshold-settings.constants.ts`). The legacy `FAILURE_THRESHOLD_COUNT` env var remains a deployment-time default for the `Count` setting; new env vars (`RETROSPECTIVE_FAILURE_THRESHOLD_*`) provide defaults for the new settings. See [§10 Failure-Threshold Settings Schema](../architecture/kanban-retrospective-cycle-decision-architecture.md#10-failure-threshold-settings-schema-wi-2026-063). |
| K5  | Is the `trigger_revision_marker` for a failure event deterministic across retried emissions? The cycle-completion path uses `cycle-2024-01-15-001` style keys. The failure path needs a deterministic, dedupe-friendly key (e.g. `failure-threshold:{project_id}:{window_start_epoch}`).                                                                                           | Medium   | **Resolved by [WI-2026-063](../work-items/WI-2026-063-failure-threshold-settings-schema.md) (work item id `2ec2799b-b003-4f5d-bca4-d56d3ef601dd`) — Deterministic revision marker.** The failure-threshold trigger emits a deterministic `trigger_revision_marker = failure-threshold:{project_id}:{window_start_epoch_seconds}`; retried emissions within the same `(project_id, window_start_epoch_seconds)` pair are automatically deduped by this key. The dedupe runs BEFORE the cooldown / bypass check, so `bypass_cooldown: true` cannot fire twice within the same window. See [§10.2 Trigger Revision Marker](../architecture/kanban-retrospective-cycle-decision-architecture.md#102-trigger-revision-marker).      |
| K6  | Where should the threshold counter be persisted? The repair lane's `publishFact` produces a fact row with an `expiresAt` of 30 minutes — suitable for a per-window counter query. The cycle-decision handler uses an in-process map which would not survive a restart; a SQL-backed counter is more durable.                                                                       | Low      | Storage decision.                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                                              |

G8–G14 are not affected by WI-2026-061.
3. Continue to enforce the R25/R30 escalation sequence for the 5 still-failed split-retries (`oauth-auth-provider`, `oauth-login-service`, `cost-governance-runtime`, `war-room-lifecycle`, `war-room-collaboration`) and the 31st-pass followup questions (R105, R106, R107, R108, R111) until each is closed by a downstream work item.

The full implementation evidence is in:

- `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-credentials-resolver.service.ts` — `GitOpsCredentialsResolver` with `resolveHttpsCredentials(binding)` and `resolveSshPrivateKey(binding)`, in-memory TTL cache, telemetry events (`gitops.credentials.resolved`, `gitops.credentials.missing`, `gitops.credentials.failed`), and a typed `CredentialResolutionError` for strict-mode failures.
- `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-invocation-builder.ts` — `GitOpsInvocationBuilder` + `buildGitHttpsAuthEnv(username, password)` helper that delivers HTTPS credentials via `GIT_CONFIG_*` env vars and SSH keys via `GIT_SSH_COMMAND` + 0600 temp file (with idempotent `cleanup` hook).
- `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-outbound-sync.service.ts` — every inline `git.exec` call now goes through `runCredentialedGit(binding, repoPath, args)` which routes via `GitOpsInvocationBuilder.build()` and awaits the `cleanup` hook in `finally`.
- `apps/api/src/gitops/desired-state-loader.service.ts` — inbound fetch/clone path now takes an optional `binding` arg and routes via the builder when present (anonymous path preserved for the deprecated env-driven `ReconciliationService` adapter).
- `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops.module.ts` — registers `GitOpsInvocationBuilder`, `GitOpsCredentialsResolver`, and `CredentialResolutionError`; env-driven `GITOPS_CREDENTIALS_OPTIONS` factory via `buildGitOpsCredentialsOptionsFromEnv()` reading `GITOPS_REQUIRE_CREDENTIALS`, `GITOPS_ANONYMOUS_ALLOWED_HOSTS`, `GITOPS_CREDENTIALS_TTL_MS`.
- `apps/api/src/gitops/gitops-outbound-sync.service.integration.spec.ts` — end-to-end integration test (AC-5) that boots the real resolver + builder with a mocked `SecretCrudService`, runs a real `git push` to a local bare repo, and asserts the credential is delivered via `GIT_CONFIG_VALUE_0` both in the invocation env and in the bare-repo `post-update` hook log. Skips cleanly when `git` is not on PATH.
- `docs/architecture/gitops.md` — design and AC traceability for the credentials feature, including the env-var contract table.
- This file (`docs/project-context/OPEN_QUESTIONS.md`) — G7 marked Resolved by WI-2026-061.

No new open questions are introduced by this resolution.

- `apps/api/src/settings/system-settings.defaults.ts` — registers the seeded defaults on boot so `SystemSettingsService.seedDefaults()` returns a sane value on a fresh database.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-failure-threshold.service.ts` — service updated to read the 6 settings at the start of every `checkFailureThreshold()` call, honor `Enabled` / `Count` / `WindowSeconds` / `WindowStrategy` / `CooldownSeconds` / `BypassCooldown`, persist the failure-window timestamp list in `orchestration.metadata.failure_threshold_timestamps`, and emit the deterministic `failure-threshold:{project_id}:{window_start_epoch_seconds}` revision marker.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-failure-threshold.types.ts` — interface updated to thread the `triggerRevisionMarker` + `idempotencyKey` + `bypassCooldown` + `windowStartEpochSeconds` payload through `runForFailureThreshold`.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-failure-threshold.helpers.ts` — pure helpers: `computeWindowStartEpochSeconds` (sliding + fixed), `pruneAndAppendFailureTimestamp`, `getFailureTimestamps`, `isCooldownActive`, `wasWindowAlreadyEmitted`.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-failure-threshold.env.ts` — env-var fallback readers (`readEnabledEnv`, `readFailureThresholdCountEnv`, `readWindowSecondsEnv`, `readCooldownSecondsEnv`, `readBypassCooldownEnv`, `readWindowStrategyEnv`) so the kanban app can run with no `SystemSettingsModule` DI wiring.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-candidate.helpers.ts` — extraction helpers that surface the `triggerRevisionMarker` on the emitted `learning.candidate.proposed.v1` event.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective.service.ts` — `executeRun` accepts the new `triggerRevisionMarker` from the caller and uses it for idempotency-key computation; emits `kanban.retrospective.cooldown_skipped` when bypass is in effect.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective-failure-threshold.service.spec.ts` — new unit tests covering each Zod-validated setting, sliding vs fixed window strategies, cooldown honored, cooldown bypassed via `BypassCooldown: true`, deterministic trigger revision marker across retried emissions, and the disabled (`Enabled: false`) no-op path.
- `apps/kanban/src/retrospectives/kanban-retrospective.integration.spec.ts` — integration spec covering the failure-threshold lifecycle (5 consecutive failures within a 60s window → fires once with a deterministic revision marker → retried emission within the cooldown is deduped → retried emission with `BypassCooldown: true` fires again).
- `apps/kanban/test/retrospectives/retrospective-failure-threshold-lifecycle.integration-spec.ts` — black-box integration test that exercises the full failure-to-retrospective path against a real database.
- `apps/kanban/test/retrospectives/retrospective-lifecycle.integration-spec.ts` — updated to thread the new `triggerRevisionMarker` + `bypassCooldown` payload through the deterministic retrospective lifecycle.
- `packages/core/src/index.ts` — re-exports the new failure-threshold-settings symbols so `@nexus/core` callers can import them.
- `docs/architecture/kanban-retrospective-cycle-decision-architecture.md` § 10 — new "Failure-Threshold Settings Schema" section documenting the 6 settings keys, sliding-vs-fixed window strategies, and trigger revision marker format.
- This file (`docs/project-context/OPEN_QUESTIONS.md`) — K2, K4, K5 marked Resolved by WI-2026-063.
